advisory <a href="https://security.archlinux.org/ASA-202501-1">ASA-202501-1</a>.</p>\n<p>An attacker only requires anonymous read access to a vulnerable rsync server, such as a public mirror, to execute arbitrary code on the machine the server is running on. \nAdditionally, attackers can take control of an affected server and read/write arbitrary files of any connected client.\nSensitive data can be extracted, such as OpenPGP and SSH keys, and malicious code can be executed by overwriting files such as <code>~/.bashrc</code> or <code>~/.popt</code>.</p>\n<p>We highly advise anyone who runs administrator to act immediately, even though the hosted package files themselves are cryptographically signed.</p>\n<p>All infrastructure servers and mirrors maintained by Arch Linux have already <code>20240301.218094</code> and <code>20240315.221711</code></li>\n<li>container images created between and including <em>2024-02-24</em> and <em>2024-03-28</em></li>\n</ul>\n<p>The affected release version!</p>\n<h2>Upgrading the system</h2>\n<p>It is strongly advised to do a full system upgrade right away if your system currently has <code>xz</code> version <code>5.6.0-1</code> or <code>5.6.1-1</code> installed:</p>\n<p><code>pacman -Syu</code></p>\n<h2>Upgrading container images</h2>\n<p>To figure out if you are using an affected container image, use either</p>\n<p><code>podman image history archlinux/archlinux</code></p>\n<p>or</p>\n<p><code>docker image history archlinux/archlinux</code></p>\n<p>depending on whether you use <code>podman</code> or <code>docker</code>.</p>\n<p>Any Arch Linux container image older than <code>2024-03-29</code> and younger than <code>2024-02-24</code> is affected.</p>\n<p>Run either</p>\n<p><code>podman image pull archlinux/archlinux</code></p>\n<p>or</p>\n<p><code>docker image pull archlinux/archlinux</code></p>\n<p>to upgrade affected container images to the most recent version.</p>\n<p>Afterwards make sure to rebuild any container images based on the affected versions and also inspect any running containers!</p>\n<h2>Regarding sshd authentication bypass/code execution</h2>\n<p>From the upstream report (<a href="https://www.openwall.com/lists/oss-security/2024/03/29/4">one</a>):</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>openssh does not directly use liblzma. However debian and several other\ndistributions patch openssh to support systemd notification, and libsystemd\ndoes depend on lzma.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Arch does not directly link openssh to liblzma, and thus this attack vector is not possible. You can confirm this by issuing the following command:</p>\n<p><code>ldd "$(command -v sshd)"</code></p>\n<p>However, out of an abundance of caution, we advise users to remove the malicious code from their system by upgrading either way.
